```bash
UID_VAL=$(git branch --show-current | sed 's/^worktree-rck-//') && echo "UID=$UID_VAL" && \

<summary>🔧 Tool: Bash -- Run ESLint on TS/TSX files and shellcheck on .sh files</summary>

**Input:**

*Run ESLint on TS/TSX files and shellcheck on .sh files*  

```bash
# Lint TypeScript files with ESLint and shell files with shellcheck
# Identify relevant files by type
TS_FILES=$(grep -E '\.(ts|tsx)$' .rechecker/files.txt | tr '\n' ' ')
SH_FILES=$(grep -E '\.sh$' .rechecker/files.txt | tr '\n' ' ')

echo "=== TypeScript/TSX files ===" > .rechecker/reports/lint-pass1.txt
echo "$TS_FILES" >> .rechecker/reports/lint-pass1.txt
echo "" >> .rechecker/reports/lint-pass1.txt

if [ -n "$TS_FILES" ]; then
  echo "=== ESLint output ===" >> .rechecker/reports/lint-pass1.txt
  npx eslint $TS_FILES --max-warnings=0 2>&1 >> .rechecker/reports/lint-pass1.txt || true
fi

echo "" >> .rechecker/reports/lint-pass1.txt
echo "=== Shell files ===" >> .rechecker/reports/lint-pass1.txt
if [ -n "$SH_FILES" ]; then
  echo "=== Shellcheck output ===" >> .rechecker/reports/lint-pass1.txt
  shellcheck $SH_FILES 2>&1 >> .rechecker/reports/lint-pass1.txt || true
fi

echo "=== Done ===" >> .rechecker/reports/lint-pass1.txt
cat .rechecker/reports/lint-pass1.txt
```

echo "=== ESLint pass ===" > .rechecker/reports/lint-pass1.txt

# Run ESLint on each TS/TSX file individually
while IFS= read -r f; do
  if [[ "$f" =~ \.(ts|tsx)$ ]] && [ -f "$f" ]; then
    echo "--- $f ---" >> .rechecker/reports/lint-pass1.txt
    npx eslint "$f" --max-warnings=0 2>&1 >> .rechecker/reports/lint-pass1.txt || true

```
function evictStaleBuildResults(): void {
  const now = Date.now()
  for (const [id, result] of buildResults) {
    const age = now - new Date(result.createdAt).getTime()
    if (age > BUILD_TTL_MS) {
      buildResults.delete(id)
      // Best-effort cleanup of build directory
      const buildDir = path.join(BUILDS_DIR, id)
      fs.rm(buildDir, { recursive: true, force: true }).catch(() => {})
    }
  }

  // If still over limit, evict oldest
  if (buildResults.size > MAX_BUILD_RESULTS) {
    const entries = [...buildResults.entries()]
      .sort((a, b) => new Date(a[1].createdAt).getTime() - new Date(b[1].createdAt).getTime())
    const toRemove = entries.slice(0, entries.length - MAX_BUILD_RESULTS)
    for (const [id] of toRemove) {
      buildResults.delete(id)
      const buildDir = path.join(BUILDS_DIR, id)
      fs.rm(buildDir, { recursive: true, force: true }).catch(() => {})
    }
  }
}
```

**New:**  
```
function evictStaleBuildResults(): void {
  const now = Date.now()
  for (const [id, result] of buildResults) {
    // Never evict an actively building entry — runBuild still holds a reference to it
    if (result.status === 'building') continue
    const age = now - new Date(result.createdAt).getTime()
    if (age > BUILD_TTL_MS) {
      buildResults.delete(id)
      // Best-effort cleanup of build directory
      const buildDir = path.join(BUILDS_DIR, id)
      fs.rm(buildDir, { recursive: true, force: true }).catch(() => {})
    }
  }

  // If still over limit, evict oldest completed/failed entries first
  if (buildResults.size > MAX_BUILD_RESULTS) {
    const entries = [...buildResults.entries()]
      .filter(([, result]) => result.status !== 'building') // Never remove active builds
      .sort((a, b) => new Date(a[1].createdAt).getTime() - new Date(b[1].createdAt).getTime())
    const toRemove = entries.slice(0, entries.lengt

... [224 more chars truncated]

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

**BUG 3: `runBuild` - unhandled promise rejection if error occurs outside the try block**  

Looking at the actual code, `runBuild` already has a `try...catch` block that wraps everything including the `execPromise` call and the stats collection (lines 564-612). The finding describes a hypothetical scenario about errors before `execPromise`, but the current code already has the outer try/catch. Let me verify the structure precisely.  

The code at line 560-613 shows `runBuild` already has:  
- `try { ... execPromise ... stats collection ... buildResults.set (complete) } catch (error) { ... buildResults.set (failed) }`  

So `runBuild` already has full try/catch coverage — the bug described in the report is not actually present. However, the report says errors would propagate as unhandled rejections. Since the function is `async` and has a top-level `try/catch`, any `await` that throws will be caught. The `.catch()` on the caller side in `buildPlugin` also catches anything that slips through. This bug is already handled correctly.  

SKIPPED BUG 3: The code already has a complete `try...catch` in `runBuild` that handles all errors. The described scenario does not apply to the current code.

The `validateBuildConfig` function doesn't validate `marketplace` name for marketplace-type skills. I need to add validation.

function validateSkillPath(skillPath: string): string | null {
  if (!skillPath || typeof skillPath !== 'string') return 'Skill path is required'
  if (skillPath.includes('..')) return 'Skill path must not contain ".."'
  if (path.isAbsolute(skillPath)) return 'Skill path must be relative'
  // Each segment must be safe
  const segments = skillPath.split('/')
  for (const seg of segments) {
    if (seg && !SAFE_PATH_SEGMENT_RE.test(seg)) {
      return `Skill path segment "${seg}" contains invalid characters`
    }
  }
  return null
}
```

**New:**  
```
function validateSkillPath(skillPath: string): string | null {
  if (!skillPath || typeof skillPath !== 'string') return 'Skill path is required'
  if (skillPath.includes('..')) return 'Skill path must not contain ".."'
  if (path.isAbsolute(skillPath)) return 'Skill path must be relative'
  // Each segment must be safe
  const segments = skillPath.split('/')
  for (const seg of segments) {
    if (seg && !SAFE_PATH_SEGMENT_RE.test(seg)) {
      return `Skill path segment "${seg}" contains invalid characters`
    }
  }
  return null
}

/**
 * Validate a marketplace name to prevent path traversal.
 * Must contain only safe characters (letters, digits, dots, hyphens, underscores).
 */
function validateMarketplaceName(name: string): string | null {
  if (!name || typeof name !== 'string') return 'Marketplace name is required'
  if (!SAFE_PATH_SEGMENT_RE.test(name)) {
    return 'Marketplace name contains invalid characters (allowed: letters, digits, dots, hyphens, underscores)'
  }
  return null
}
```

  for (const skill of config.skills) {
    if (skill.type === 'repo') {
      const urlErr = validateGitUrl(skill.url)

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 23:44:46]*

**Old:**  
```
  } catch (error: unknown) {
    // Clean up on error
    await fs.rm(scanDir, { recursive: true, force: true }).catch(() => {})

    const exitCode = (error as any)?.code
    const message = error instanceof Error ? error.message : String(error)

    if (exitCode === 128 || message.includes('not found')) {
      return { error: `Repository not found or access denied: ${url}`, status: 404 }
    }
    console.error('Error scanning repo:', error)

  }
}

**New:**  
```
  } catch (error: unknown) {
    // Clean up on error
    await fs.rm(scanDir, { recursive: true, force: true }).catch(() => {})

    const exitCode = (error as any)?.code
    let message = error instanceof Error ? error.message : String(error)
    const stderr = (error as any)?.stderr
    // Include stderr in the message so callers get the full git error detail
    if (stderr) message += `\nDetails: ${stderr}`

    if (exitCode === 128 || message.includes('not found')) {
      return { error: `Repository not found or access denied: ${url}`, status: 404 }
    }
    console.error('Error scanning repo:', error)
    return { error: `Failed to scan repository: ${message}`, status: 500 }
  } finally {
    activeOps = Math.max(0, activeOps - 1)
  }
}
```

    console.error('Error pushing to GitHub:', error)
    return { error: `Failed to push to GitHub: ${message}`, status: 500 }
  } finally {
    activeOps = Math.max(0, activeOps - 1)
  }
}
```

   189→function evictStaleBuildResults(): void {  
   190→  const now = Date.now()  
   191→  for (const [id, result] of buildResults) {  
   192→    // Never evict an actively building entry — runBuild still holds a reference to it  
   193→    if (result.status === 'building') continue  
   194→    const age = now - new Date(result.createdAt).getTime()  
   195→    if (age > BUILD_TTL_MS) {  
   196→      buildResults.delete(id)  
   197→      // Best-effort cleanup of build directory  
   198→      const buildDir = path.join(BUILDS_DIR, id)  
   199→      fs.rm(buildDir, { recursive: true, force: true }).catch(() => {})  
   200→    }  
   201→  }  
   202→  
   203→  // If still over limit, evict oldest completed/failed entries first  
   204→  if (buildResults.size > MAX_BUILD_RESULTS) {  
   205→    const entries = [...buildResults.entries()]  
   206→      .filter(([, result]) => result.status !== 'building') // Never remove active builds  
   207→      .sort((a, b) => new Date(a[1].createdAt).getTime() - new Date(b[1].createdAt).getTime())  
   208→    const toRemove = entries.slice(0, entries.length - MAX_BUILD_RESULTS)  
   209→    for (const [id] of toRemove) {  
   210→      buildResults.delete(id)  
   211→      const buildDir = path.join(BUILDS_DIR, id)  
   212→      fs.rm(buildDir, { recursive: true, force: true }).catch(() => {})  
   213→    }  
   214→  }  
   215→}  
   216→  
   217→// Run eviction every 10 minutes  
   218→const evictionInterval = setInterval(evictStaleBuildResults, 10 * 60 * 1000)

Fix bugs in: components/plugin-builder/SkillPicker.tsx — Read findings from: .rechecker/reports/rck-20260322_235008_eead5d-[LP00002-IT00002-FID00011]-review.md  

The bug: `RepoScanner`'s `onSkillsFound` prop has signature `(skills: RepoSkillInfo[], url: string, ref: string) => void` but SkillPicker passes `(skills) => setRepoSkillsCount(skills.length)` which only accepts 1 argument. Fix: update the callback to accept all 3 parameters: `(skills, _url, _ref) => setRepoSkillsCount(skills.length)`.  

First read components/plugin-builder/RepoScanner.tsx to confirm the actual interface, then fix SkillPicker.tsx accordingly.  

REPORTING RULES:  
- Return ONLY: "[DONE/FAILED] fix FID00011-IT2 - brief_result"  
- Max 2 lines back to orchestrator

**Result:**

   165→  
   166→### BUG: `pm2 restart all` fallback is too broad  
   167→**Severity**: low  
   168→**Location**: `act4_start_and_register`  
   169→**Problem**: In `act4_start_and_register`, when updating and restarting the service, the command `pm2 restart ai-maestro 2>/dev/null || pm2 restart all 2>/dev/null || true` is used. The fallback `pm2 restart all` is too broad. If `pm2 restart ai-maestro` fails, `pm2 restart all` will attempt to restart every single process managed by PM2, which might include unrelated services. This is an undesirable side effect for an installer script.  
   170→**Fix**: The fallback should be more specific, or the error handling for `pm2 restart ai-maestro` should be improved. If `pm2 restart ai-maestro` fails, it's better to report that specific failure rather than attempting to restart all services. A more robust approach would be to check if `ai-maestro` is actually managed by PM2 before attempting to restart it, and if not, fall back to the `nohup` restart logic.  
   171→  
   172→```bash  
   173→            cd "$INSTALL_DIR"  
   174→            if command -v pm2 &>/dev/null; then  
   175→                # Check if ai-maestro is actually managed by pm2  
   176→                if pm2 list | grep -q "ai-maestro"; then  
   177→                    pm2 restart ai-maestro 2>/dev/null || maestro_warn "Failed to restart AI Maestro via PM2. Please check PM2 logs."  
   178→                else  
   179→                    # Fallback to nohup restart logic if not managed by pm2  
   180→                    local old_pid  
   181→                    old_pid=$(lsof -ti:"$PORT" 2>/dev/null || true)  
   182→                    if [ -n "$old_pid" ]; then  
   183→                        kill "$old_pid" 2>/dev/null || true  
   184→                        sleep 2  
   185→                    fi  
   186→                    mkdir -p "$INSTALL_DIR/logs"  
   187→                    nohup yarn start > "$INSTALL_DIR/logs/startup.log" 2>&1 &  
   188→                fi  
   189→              

... [3195 more chars truncated]

            kill "$pid_to_kill" 2>/dev/null || true
            maestro_info "Stopped nohup AI Maestro process (PID: $pid_to_kill)"
        fi
        rm -f "$INSTALL_DIR/logs/aimaestro.pid" 2>/dev/null || true
    fi

    # Stop PM2 services if running
    if command -v pm2 &>/dev/null; then
        pm2 stop ai-maestro 2>/dev/null || true

```

**New:**  
```
            cd "$INSTALL_DIR"
            if command -v pm2 &>/dev/null; then
                # Only restart the specific ai-maestro process; never restart all PM2 processes
                if pm2 list 2>/dev/null | grep -q "ai-maestro"; then
                    pm2 restart ai-maestro 2>/dev/null || maestro_warn "Failed to restart AI Maestro via PM2 — check: pm2 logs ai-maestro"
                else
                    # ai-maestro is not managed by PM2; fall through to nohup restart
                    local old_pid
                    old_pid=$(lsof -ti:"$PORT" 2>/dev/null || true)
                    if [ -n "$old_pid" ]; then
                        kill "$old_pid" 2>/dev/null || true
                        sleep 2
                    fi
                    mkdir -p "$INSTALL_DIR/logs"
                    nohup yarn start > "$INSTALL_DIR/logs/startup.log" 2>&1 &
                    echo $! > "$INSTALL_DIR/logs/aimaestro.pid"
                fi
            else
```

**Result:**

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The `description` field in `PluginBuildConfig` is typed as `description?: string` (optional). This means `undefined` is the correct representation for an absent description. The current `description || undefined` logic is almost correct but fails to trim whitespace — `"  "` (spaces only) would pass through as a non-empty string. The proper fix is `description.trim() || undefined`.  

Now I'll apply both fixes:  

**Fix 1:** `description` — use `description.trim() || undefined` for consistent trimmed empty-string-to-undefined conversion.  

**Fix 2:** Regex — change `^[a-zA-Z0-9][a-zA-Z0-9_-]*$` to `^[a-zA-Z0-9]+(?:[_-][a-zA-Z0-9]+)*$` in both `isValid` and `disabledReason`.  

</div>

    15→  
    16→    if (!body.forkUrl || typeof body.forkUrl !== 'string') {  
    17→      return NextResponse.json(

    19→        { status: 400 }  
    20→      )  
    21→    }

    28→      )

    46→    return NextResponse.json(

   270→// Utility helpers  
   271→// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------  
   272→  
   273→async function readJsonBody(req: IncomingMessage): Promise<any> {  
   274→  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {  
   275→    const chunks: Buffer[] = []  
   276→    req.on('data', (chunk: Buffer) => chunks.push(chunk))  
   277→    req.on('end', () => {  
   278→      const body = Buffer.concat(chunks).toString('utf-8')  
   279→      if (!body) return resolve({})  
   280→      try {  
   281→        resolve(JSON.parse(body))  
   282→      } catch (e) {  
   283→        reject(new Error('Invalid JSON body'))  
   284→      }  
   285→    })  
   286→    req.on('error', reject)  
   287→  })  
   288→}  
   289→  
   290→async function readRawBody(req: IncomingMessage): Promise<Buffer> {  
   291→  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {  
   292→    const chunks: Buffer[] = []  
   293→    req.on('data', (chunk: Buffer) => chunks.push(chunk))  
   294→    req.on('end', () => resolve(Buffer.concat(chunks)))  
   295→    req.on('error', reject)  
   296→  })  
   297→}  
   298→  
   299→function sendJson(res: ServerResponse, statusCode: number, data: any, headers?: Record<string, string>) {  
   300→  const body = JSON.stringify(data)  
   301→  res.writeHead(statusCode, {  
   302→    'Content-Type': 'application/json',  
   303→    'Content-Length': Buffer.byteLength(body),  
   304→    ...headers,  
   305→  })  
   306→  res.end(body)  
   307→}  
   308→  
   309→function sendBinary(res: ServerResponse, statusCode: number, buffer: Buffer | Uint8Array, headers: Record<string, string>) {  
   310→  res.writeHead(statusCode, headers)  
   311→  res.end(buffer)  
   312→}

   314→function sendServiceResult(res: ServerResponse, result: any) {

   317→  } else {  
   318→    sendJson(res, result.status || 200, result.data, result.headers)  
   319→  }  
   320→}

  1249→function matchRoute(method: string, pathname: string): { handler: RouteHandler; params: Record<string, string> } | null {  
  1250→  for (const route of routes) {  
  1251→    if (route.method !== method) continue  
  1252→  
  1253→    const match = pathname.match(route.pattern)  
  1254→    if (!match) continue  
  1255→  
  1256→    const params: Record<string, string> = {}  
  1257→    route.paramNames.forEach((name, i) => {  
  1258→      params[name] = match[i + 1]  
  1259→    })  
  1260→  
  1261→    return { handler: route.handler, params }  
  1262→  }  
  1263→  return null  
  1264→}  
  1265→  
  1266→export function createHeadlessRouter() {  
  1267→  return {  
  1268→    async handle(req: IncomingMessage, res: ServerResponse): Promise<boolean> {  
  1269→      const parsedUrl = parse(req.url || '', true)  
  1270→      const pathname = parsedUrl.pathname || '/'  
  1271→      const method = req.method || 'GET'  
  1272→      const query = getQuery(req.url || '')  
  1273→  
  1274→      const matched = matchRoute(method, pathname)  
  1275→      if (!matched) {  
  1276→        return false // Not handled — caller should return 404  
  1277→      }  
  1278→  
  1279→      try {  
  1280→        await matched.handler(req, res, matched.params, query)  
  1281→      } catch (error) {  
  1282→        console.error(`[Headless] Error handling ${method} ${pathname}:`, error)  
  1283→        if (!res.headersSent) {  
  1284→          sendJson(res, 500, { error: 'Internal server error' })  
  1285→        }  
  1286→      }  
  1287→  
  1288→      return true // Handled  
  1289→    },  
  1290→  }  
  1291→}

**BUG 1** (medium): `handle` function — when `res.headersSent` is true after an error, the connection is left hanging. Fix: call `res.end()` in that case.

Wait — actually since these are `async` handlers and the catch block is the last thing (the function just returns after the catch), there's no code after the catch to fall through to. The outer router catches exceptions thrown from handlers, but `sendJson` in the catch doesn't throw. So the handler returns normally after the catch. The report's concern about "continuing execution" is not actually valid here because there's no code after the catch block. However, it's still good defensive practice to add `return`.

        await matched.handler(req, res, matched.params, query)

        console.error(`[Headless] Error handling ${method} ${pathname}:`, error)

          // Headers already sent — cannot change status code. End the response to prevent a hanging connection.
          console.warn(`[Headless] Headers already sent for ${method} ${pathname}, cannot send proper error response.`)

function sendServiceResult(res: ServerResponse, result: any) {
  if (result.error && !result.data) {
    sendJson(res, result.status || 500, { error: result.error }, result.headers)
  } else {
    sendJson(res, result.status || 200, result.data, result.headers)

}
```

**New:**  
```
function sendServiceResult(res: ServerResponse, result: any) {
  if (result.error && !result.data) {
    // Ensure the error is a serializable string — Error objects serialize to {} via JSON.stringify
    const errorMessage = result.error instanceof Error ? result.error.message : result.error
    sendJson(res, result.status || 500, { error: errorMessage }, result.headers)
  } else {
    sendJson(res, result.status || 200, result.data, result.headers)
  }
}
```

**New:**  
```
function parseMultipart(body: Buffer, contentType: string): { file: Buffer | null; options: string | null } {
  const boundaryMatch = contentType.match(/boundary=([^\s;]+)/)
  // Throw so the caller's catch block can report a meaningful 400 error rather than silently returning nulls
  if (!boundaryMatch) throw new BadRequestError('Invalid or missing boundary in Content-Type header for multipart/form-data')
```

  { method: 'POST', pattern: /^\/api\/agents\/import$/, paramNames: [], handler: async (req, res) => {

      const rawBody = await readRawBody(req)
      const { file, options: optionsStr } = parseMultipart(rawBody, contentType)

      if (!file) {
        sendJson(res, 400, { error: 'No file provided' })

      const result = await importAgent(file, options)

**New:**  
```
  { method: 'POST', pattern: /^\/api\/agents\/import$/, paramNames: [], handler: async (req, res) => {
    try {
      const contentType = getHeader(req, 'content-type') || ''
      const rawBody = await readRawBody(req)
      // parseMultipart throws BadRequestError on invalid/missing boundary
      const { file, options: optionsStr } = parseMultipart(rawBody, contentType)

      if (!file) {
        sendJson(res, 400, { error: 'No file provided in multipart form data' })
        return
      }

      let options = {}
      if (optionsStr) {
        try {
          options = JSON.parse(optionsStr)
        } catch {
          // Invalid JSON in the options field is a client error — return 400
          sendJson(res, 400, { error: 'Invalid JSON in options field' })
          return
        }
      }

      const result = await importAgent(file, options)
      sendServiceResult(res, result)
    } catch (error) {
      if (error instanceof BadRequestError) {
        sendJson(res, 400, { error: error.message })
      } else {
        sendJson(res, 500, { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Unknown error' })
      }
    }
  }},
```

**Result:**

   269→// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------  
   270→// Error types  
   271→// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------  
   272→  
   273→/** Thrown for client-caused errors (malformed request). The router maps this to HTTP 400. */  
   274→class BadRequestError extends Error {  
   275→  constructor(message: string) {  
   276→    super(message)  
   277→    this.name = 'BadRequestError'  
   278→  }  
   279→}  
   280→  
   281→// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------  
   282→// Utility helpers  
   283→// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------  
   284→  
   285→async function readJsonBody(req: IncomingMessage): Promise<any> {  
   286→  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {  
   287→    const chunks: Buffer[] = []  
   288→    req.on('data', (chunk: Buffer) => chunks.push(chunk))  
   289→    req.on('end', () => {  
   290→      const body = Buffer.concat(chunks).toString('utf-8')  
   291→      if (!body) return resolve({})

   296→        reject(new BadRequestError('Invalid JSON body'))

   299→    req.on('error', reject)

   302→  
   303→async function readRawBody(req: IncomingMessage): Promise<Buffer> {  
   304→  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {  
   305→    const chunks: Buffer[] = []  
   306→    req.on('data', (chunk: Buffer) => chunks.push(chunk))  
   307→    req.on('end', () => resolve(Buffer.concat(chunks)))  
   308→    req.on('error', reject)  
   309→  })  
   310→}

   327→function sendServiceResult(res: ServerResponse, result: any) {  
   328→  if (result.error && !result.data) {  
   329→    // Ensure the error is a serializable string — Error objects serialize to {} via JSON.stringify

   332→  } else {

   337→function getHeader(req: IncomingMessage, name: string): string | null {  
   338→  const val = req.headers[name.toLowerCase()]  
   339→  return typeof val === 'string' ? val : null

   341→  
   342→function getQuery(url: string): Record<string, string> {  
   343→  const parsed = parse(url, true)  
   344→  const q: Record<string, string> = {}  
   345→  for (const [k, v] of Object.entries(parsed.query)) {  
   346→    if (typeof v === 'string') q[k] = v  
   347→  }  
   348→  return q  
   349→}

  1299→export function createHeadlessRouter() {  
  1300→  return {  
  1301→    async handle(req: IncomingMessage, res: ServerResponse): Promise<boolean> {  
  1302→      const parsedUrl = parse(req.url || '', true)  
  1303→      const pathname = parsedUrl.pathname || '/'  
  1304→      const method = req.method || 'GET'  
  1305→      const query = getQuery(req.url || '')  
  1306→  
  1307→      const matched = matchRoute(method, pathname)  
  1308→      if (!matched) {  
  1309→        return false // Not handled — caller should return 404  
  1310→      }  
  1311→  
  1312→      try {  
  1313→        await matched.handler(req, res, matched.params, query)  
  1314→      } catch (error) {  
  1315→        console.error(`[Headless] Error handling ${method} ${pathname}:`, error)  
  1316→        if (res.headersSent) {  
  1317→          // Headers already sent — cannot change status code. End the response to prevent a hanging connection.  
  1318→          console.warn(`[Headless] Headers already sent for ${method} ${pathname}, cannot send proper error response.`)  
  1319→          res.end()  
  1320→        } else if (error instanceof BadRequestError) {  
  1321→          sendJson(res, 400, { error: error.message })  
  1322→        } else {  
  1323→          sendJson(res, 500, { error: 'Internal server error' })  
  1324→        }

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 23:43:54]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have complete context. Let me analyze the bugs:  

1. **BUG: `getSkillKey` for `repo` type is incomplete** - The key is `repo:${skill.url}:${skill.skillPath}` but the type has a `ref` field that distinguishes branches/tags/commits. Two skills from the same URL and path but different refs produce identical keys. Fix: include `ref` in the key.  

2. **BUG: Marketplace skills count in tabs is not dynamic for filtered results** - The `count` for the `core` tab uses `CORE_SKILLS.length` (total, not filtered) and `marketplace` tab uses `marketplaceSkills.length` (total, not filtered). When a search is active, the counts are misleading. Fix: use `filteredCoreSkills.length` and `filteredMarketplaceSkills.length`.  

3. **BUG: `RepoScanner` `onSkillsFound` callback is a no-op** - The `onSkillsFound` signature from `RepoScanner` is `(skills: RepoSkillInfo[], url: string, ref: string) => void` and the current pass `() => {}` silently drops found skills data. This is genuinely a functional bug since `onSkillsFound` is called right after a successful scan and the SkillPicker never knows about the scanned skills. Fix: The `SkillPicker` should track scanned repo skills to show the count on the tab, matching the design pattern of the other tabs.  

4. **BUG: Missing dependency** - The useEffect has an empty dependency array which is correct here (intentional run-once fetch with abort on cleanup). This is not a real bug — `setMarketplaceSkills` and `setLoadingMarketplace` are stable setState functions, so the lint rule is not actually violated. This reported finding is not a real bug and doesn't need a fix.  

Now I'll apply the fixes:  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 23:52:01]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have the full picture. The `PluginSkillSelection` type for `marketplace` is:

The type guarantees `marketplace` and `plugin` are always present (non-optional strings), so `getSkillSubtitle` is safe. However, the `id` field for `marketplace` skills — there's no guarantee it has two colons. ## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 23:43:54]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have the complete picture. From `MarketplaceSkill`:  
- `id` format is `marketplace:plugin:skill` (the comment says "Unique ID: marketplace:plugin:skill")  
- `name` is a string property on `MarketplaceSkill`  

The problem is clear: when `SkillPicker.tsx` creates a `PluginSkillSelection` of type `marketplace`, it only passes `id`, `marketplace`, and `plugin` — it does NOT pass `name` from `MarketplaceSkill`. The `PluginSkillSelection` type for `marketplace` does not include a `name` field.  

So in `getSkillDisplayName`, `skill.id.split(':')[2]` extracts the third segment (the skill part) from `marketplace:plugin:skill`. Since the comment in `MarketplaceSkill` confirms the format is exactly `marketplace:plugin:skill`, this works — but `split(':')[2]` can still be `undefined` if `id` doesn't have two colons (e.g., just `skillname`).  

Using `split(':').pop()` would be safer — it returns the last segment regardless of how many colons are present, and for a well-formed ID it returns the same result, but it never returns `undefined` (always returns at least the whole string if there are no colons).  

For `getSkillSubtitle`, since `marketplace` and `plugin` are non-optional in the type definition, there's no null risk. However, since both are guaranteed to be strings (they are both required in the discriminated union), no fallback is needed.  

The only real bug is in `getSkillDisplayName`: `skill.id.split(':')[2]` returns `undefined` when the id doesn't contain two colons, and the fallback `|| skill.id` would then show the raw composite id (e.g., `marketplace:plugin:skillname`) instead of just the skill name. The fix is to use `.pop()` for robustness.  

Now let me apply the fix:  

</div>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 23:43:55]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `PluginComposer.tsx`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-eead5d/components/plugin-builder/PluginComposer.tsx`  

**Old:**  
```
    case 'marketplace':
      return skill.id.split(':')[2] || skill.id
```

**New:**  
```
    case 'marketplace':
      // skill.id format is "marketplace:plugin:skillName"; pop() returns the last segment
      // regardless of how many colons are present, avoiding undefined from split()[2]
      return skill.id.split(':').pop() || skill.id
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-eead5d/components/plugin-builder/PluginComposer.tsx has been updated successfully.  

</details>

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 23:44:03]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The fix is correct. `getSkillSubtitle` is sound — `marketplace` and `plugin` are non-optional required string fields in the discriminated union type, so no fix needed there.

**Bug 1 (medium):** `handleBuild` — when `data.status !== 'building'` on initial response, `setBuilding(false)` is missing in the `else` branch. **Bug 9: `AI_TOOL` in tmux commands** - Lines 1319 and 1329-1330: `"$AI_TOOL \"$INITIAL_PROMPT\""` - `$AI_TOOL` is inside double quotes so it IS effectively quoted as a single argument to the shell. But the issue is it's used as the command string passed to tmux, which interprets it via shell. This is actually correct as-is.  

**Bug 10: `nvm use 20 || true`** - Line 702: `nvm use 20 >/dev/null 2>&1 || true` - remove `|| true` to let errors surface.  

**Bug 11/12: `pm2 save 2>/dev/null`** - Lines 372 and 1174: remove `2>/dev/null` from `pm2 save` calls.

     2→ * Plugin Builder - Push to GitHub API

     9→import { pushToGitHub } from '@/services/plugin-builder-service'  
    10→import type { PluginPushConfig } from '@/types/plugin-builder'  
    11→  
    12→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
    13→  try {  
    14→    const body = await request.json() as PluginPushConfig  
    15→  
    16→    if (!body.forkUrl || typeof body.forkUrl !== 'string') {  
    17→      return NextResponse.json(  
    18→        { error: 'Fork URL is required' },  
    19→        { status: 400 }  
    20→      )  
    21→    }  
    22→  
    23→    if (!body.manifest || typeof body.manifest !== 'object') {  
    24→      return NextResponse.json(

    26→        { status: 400 }  
    27→      )  
    28→    }  
    29→  
    30→    const result = await pushToGitHub(body)  
    31→  
    32→    if (result.error) {  
    33→      return NextResponse.json(  
    34→        { error: result.error },  
    35→        { status: result.status }  
    36→      )  
    37→    }  
    38→    return NextResponse.json(result.data)  
    39→  } catch (error) {  
    40→    console.error('Error pushing to GitHub:', error)  
    41→    return NextResponse.json(  
    42→      { error: 'Invalid request body' },  
    43→      { status: 400 }  
    44→    )  
    45→  }  
    46→}

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 23:43:29]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have the full picture. The `ServiceResult<T>` type has `status: number` (not optional), so `result.status` is always a number. However, looking at the source carefully:  

1. **BUG 1 (medium - critical path)**: `result.status` could be any number returned from `pushToGitHub`. The type says `status: number` but the route uses it directly without validating it's a proper HTTP status code. In practice all paths in `pushToGitHub` return valid codes (400, 429, 500, 200), BUT when `result.error` is set, `result.status` could be anything returned. The fix is to guard it.  

2. **BUG 2 (low)**: Generic error message - the finding says no code change strictly necessary, I'll skip this non-actionable one.  

3. **BUG 3 (low)**: Missing `Array.isArray` check on manifest validation - an array `typeof` returns `'object'` so an array would pass the current check but cause downstream failures.  

Let me now apply the real fixes:  

</div>

    if (!body.manifest || typeof body.manifest !== 'object') {
      return NextResponse.json(

      )
    }

**New:**  
```
    // Array.isArray guard: typeof [] === 'object', which would pass a bare object check
    if (!body.manifest || typeof body.manifest !== 'object' || Array.isArray(body.manifest)) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: 'Manifest is required and must be an object' },
        { status: 400 }
      )
    }

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 23:43:23]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

This is critical context. The project uses Next.js **14.2.35**, but many route files already use `Promise<{ id: string }>` for params. In Next.js 14, params is NOT a Promise — the `Promise` typing is a Next.js 15+ pattern. The reviewer correctly identified this as a bug. However, I need to check whether this `Promise` pattern is consistently used everywhere in this codebase, or if there's a mix — because if it's consistent throughout the entire project, then either: (a) it's a widespread copy-paste bug throughout the whole codebase, or (b) there's a reason for it.  

Let me check one of the plain-object routes vs the Promise routes more carefully and also check the Next.js version being actively compiled against:  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 23:43:34]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

There's a mix: 101 files use `Promise<params>` and a few use the plain object pattern. The plain object pattern is correct for Next.js 14. The `Promise` pattern is incorrect for Next.js 14 — it's the Next.js 15 API. However, `await`-ing a plain object in JS/TS is a no-op (it resolves immediately to the object itself), so `await params` on a plain object won't throw — it just returns the object. The **actual problem** is the type declaration being wrong, which could cause TypeScript errors or mislead the type checker.  

The finding report is focused specifically on the file `app/api/plugin-builder/builds/[id]/route.ts`. The fix is to change the `params` type from `Promise<{ id: string }>` to `{ id: string }` and remove the `await`. This is the correct fix for Next.js 14.  

However, since 101 other files have the same pattern, I must fix all of them too — the instructions say "check if the same pattern appears elsewhere in the file — fix all occurrences" and "similar instances of the same error type". But those 101 files are outside the target file. The instructions also say "You must always examine not only the code affected by the issue but also search for similar instances of the same error type."  

Let me fix the target file first, then address all other files with the same bug:  

</div>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 23:43:35]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `route.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-eead5d/app/api/plugin-builder/builds/[id]/route.ts`  

**Old:**  
```
export async function GET(
  _request: NextRequest,
  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }
) {
  const { id } = await params
```

**New:**  
```
export async function GET(
  _request: NextRequest,
  { params }: { params: { id: string } }
) {
  const { id } = params
```

     1→import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     2→import {  
     3→  getAgentSessionStatus,

     8→  
     9→/**  
    10→ * POST /api/agents/[id]/session  
    11→ * Link a tmux session to an agent  
    12→ */  
    13→export async function POST(  
    14→  request: Request,  
    15→  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }  
    16→) {  
    17→  const { id } = await params  
    18→  const body = await request.json()  
    19→  const result = linkAgentSession(id, body)  
    20→  
    21→  if (result.error) {  
    22→    return NextResponse.json({ error: result.error }, { status: result.status })  
    23→  }  
    24→  return NextResponse.json(result.data)  
    25→}  
    26→  
    27→/**  
    28→ * PATCH /api/agents/[id]/session  
    29→ * Send a command to the agent's tmux session  
    30→ */  
    31→export async function PATCH(  
    32→  request: NextRequest,  
    33→  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }  
    34→) {  
    35→  const { id } = await params  
    36→  const body = await request.json()  
    37→  
    38→  const result = await sendAgentSessionCommand(id, {  
    39→    command: body.command,  
    40→    requireIdle: body.requireIdle,  
    41→    addNewline: body.addNewline,  
    42→  })  
    43→  
    44→  if (result.error && result.status !== 409) {  
    45→    return NextResponse.json(  
    46→      { success: false, error: result.error },  
    47→      { status: result.status }  
    48→    )  
    49→  }  
    50→  
    51→  // For 409 (not idle), include data + error together  
    52→  if (result.status === 409) {  
    53→    return NextResponse.json(  
    54→      { success: false, error: result.error, ...result.data },  
    55→      { status: 409 }  
    56→    )  
    57→  }  
    58→  
    59→  return NextResponse.json(result.data)

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 23:44:26]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

I notice that `sessions/[id]/rename/route.ts` has a special case: it uses `await Promise.all([request.json(), params])` — treating `params` as a Promise directly. This is the only file that actually *relies* on params being awaitable. In Next.js 14 where params is a plain object, `await plainObject` resolves immediately, so this still works correctly — but the type annotation is wrong and must be fixed.  

Now I'll read the remaining files:  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 23:47:00]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I need to handle the special case in `sessions/[id]/rename/route.ts` — it uses `await Promise.all([request.json(), params])`, treating `params` as a Promise. Since params is now a plain object (not a Promise), `await plainObject` still resolves correctly to the object itself in JS, so this code is functionally fine. But I should clean it up to be consistent:  

</div>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 23:47:01]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `route.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-eead5d/app/api/sessions/[id]/rename/route.ts"
}
```

**Result:**

     1→import { NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     2→import { renameSession } from '@/services/sessions-service'  
     3→  
     4→export const dynamic = 'force-dynamic'  
     5→  
     6→/**  
     7→ * @deprecated Use PATCH /api/agents/[id] to update agent alias instead.  
     8→ * This endpoint uses tmux session names directly, while the agent endpoint  
     9→ * uses agent IDs for proper multi-host support.  
    10→ */  
    11→function logDeprecation() {  
    12→  console.warn('[DEPRECATED] PATCH /api/sessions/[id]/rename - Use PATCH /api/agents/[id] to update alias instead')  
    13→}  
    14→  
    15→export async function PATCH(  
    16→  request: Request,  
    17→  { params }: { params: { id: string } }  
    18→) {  
    19→  logDeprecation()  
    20→  try {  
    21→    const [{ newName }, { id: oldName }] = await Promise.all([  
    22→      request.json(),  
    23→      params  
    24→    ])  
    25→  
    26→    const result = await renameSession(oldName, newName)  
    27→  
    28→    if (result.error) {  
    29→      return NextResponse.json({ error: result.error }, { status: result.status })  
    30→    }  
    31→  
    32→    return NextResponse.json(result.data, { status: result.status })  
    33→  } catch (error) {  
    34→    console.error('Failed to rename session:', error)  
    35→    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Failed to rename session' }, { status: 500 })  
    36→  }  
    37→}  
    38→  

[system reminder collapsed]  


</details>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 23:47:07]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The type is already fixed. Now the `await Promise.all([request.json(), params])` usage is still valid — `await`-ing a plain object in a `Promise.all` is fine since `Promise.all` accepts non-Promise values and resolves them immediately. However, this is a bit odd since `params` is no longer a Promise. The clean fix is to destructure `params` directly and only `await` the async operation:  

</div>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 23:47:08]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `route.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-eead5d/app/api/sessions/[id]/rename/route.ts`  

**Old:**  
```
    const [{ newName }, { id: oldName }] = await Promise.all([
      request.json(),
      params
    ])
```

**New:**  
```
    const { newName } = await request.json()
    const { id: oldName } = params
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-eead5d/app/api/sessions/[id]/rename/route.ts has been updated successfully.  

</details>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 23:47:12]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 23:34:43]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The SC2015 warning: `A && B || C` — the issue is that if `A` succeeds but `B` fails, `C` will run unexpectedly. In these cases:  
- `A` = `_install_npm_global ...` (npm install)  
- `B` = `{ maestro_ok ...; HAS_CLAUDE=true; NEED_CLAUDE=false; }` (block of simple echo/variable assignments — these cannot fail)  
- `C` = the error handler block  

The `B` block contains only `maestro_ok` (which is a `printf` — cannot fail), `HAS_CLAUDE=true` (variable assignment — cannot fail), and `NEED_CLAUDE=false` (variable assignment — cannot fail). So `B` will NEVER fail, meaning C will never run incorrectly. The pattern is actually safe here.  

The correct approach is to use `if/then/else` to make the intent explicit and eliminate the warning properly — not add a comment (that's a workaround/hack). Let me restructure these as proper `if/then/else` constructs.  

Now I'll apply all fixes:  

</div>
